href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">\n          question marks, boxes, or other symbols\n         </a>\n         instead of\n         <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">\n          Unicode\n         </a>\n         characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">\n          Help:IPA\n         </a>\n         .\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Portuguese\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         portugu\xc3\xaas\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       or, in full,\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         l\xc3\xadngua portuguesa\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ) is a western\n       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">\n        Romance language\n       </a>\n       and the sole official language of\n       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">\n        Portugal\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">\n        Brazil\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">\n        Cape Verde\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">\n        Guinea-Bissau\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">\n        Mozambique\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">\n        Angola\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="S\xc3\xa3o Tom\xc3\xa9 and Pr\xc3\xadncipe">\n        S\xc3\xa3o Tom\xc3\xa9 and Pr\xc3\xadncipe\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPLP_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CPLP-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It also has co-official language status in\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">\n        East Timor\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">\n        Equatorial Guinea\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">\n        Macau\n       </a>\n       in China. As the result of expansion during colonial times, a cultural presence of Portuguese and\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-based_creole_languages" title="Portuguese-based creole languages">\n        Portuguese creole\n       </a>\n       speakers are also found in\n       <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">\n        Goa\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">\n        Daman and Diu\n       </a>\n       in India;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Batticaloa" title="Batticaloa">\n        Batticaloa\n       </a>\n       on the east coast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">\n        Sri Lanka\n       </a>\n       ; in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">\n        Indonesian\n       </a>\n       island of\n       <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">\n        Flores\n       </a>\n       ; in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">\n        Malacca\n       </a>\n       state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">\n        Malaysia\n       </a>\n       ; and the\n       <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">\n        ABC islands\n       </a>\n       in the Caribbean where\n       <a href="/wiki/Papiamento" title="Papiamento">\n        Papiamento\n       </a>\n       is spoken, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">\n        Cape Verdean Creole\n       </a>\n       is the most widely spoken Portuguese-based Creole. A Portuguese-speaking person or nation may be referred to as "\n       <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">\n        Lusophone\n       </a>\n       " in both English and Portuguese.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese is part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">\n        Ibero-Romance group\n       </a>\n       that evolved from several dialects of\n       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">\n        Vulgar Latin\n       </a>\n       in the medieval\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Kingdom of Galicia">\n        Kingdom of Galicia\n       </a>\n       , and has kept some\n       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">\n        Celtic\n       </a>\n       phonology and lexicon.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       With approximately 215 to 220 million native speakers and 260 million total speakers, Portuguese is usually listed as the sixth\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">\n        most natively spoken language\n       </a>\n       in the world, the third-most spoken European language in the world in terms of native speakers,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and a major language of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">\n        Southern Hemisphere\n       </a>\n       . It is also the most spoken language in South America and the second-most spoken in Latin America after Spanish, and is an official language of the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">\n        European Union\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mercosul" title="Mercosul">\n        Mercosul\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States#Official_languages" title="Organization of American States">\n        OAS\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">\n        ECOWAS\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">\n        African Union\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           History\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2">\n         <a href="#Geographic_distribution">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Geographic distribution\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3">\n           <a href="#Official_status">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Official status\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4">\n           <a class="toctext">\n             Population of countries and jurisdictions of Portuguese official or co-official language\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li           <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Future\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n class="toctext">\n           Dialects\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n           <a href="#Brazil">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Brazil\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-9">\n           <a href="#Portugal">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Portugal\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n           <a href="#Other_countries_and_dependencies">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Other countries and dependencies\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">\n           <a href="#Characterization_and_peculiarities">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Characterization and peculiarities\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">\n         <a href="#Vocabulary">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Vocabulary\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13">\n         <a href="#Classification_and_related_languages">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Classification and related languages\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#Galician-Portuguese_in_Spain">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Galician-Portuguese in Spain\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Influence_on_other_languages">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Influence on other languages\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Derived_languages">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Derived languages\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#Phonology">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Phonology\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#Vowels">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Vowels\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Consonants">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Consonants\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20">\n         <a href="#Grammar">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Grammar\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21">\n         <a href="#Writing_system">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Writing system\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22">\n           <a href="#Spelling_reforms">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Spelling reforms\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a href="#Literature">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Literature\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Phonology.2C_orthography_and_grammar">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Phonology, orthography and grammar\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27">\n           <a href="#Reference_dictionaries">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Reference dictionaries\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28">\n           <a href="#Linguistic_studies">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Linguistic studies\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Portuguese_language" title="History of the Portuguese language">\n        History of the Portuguese language\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       When the Romans arrived in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">\n        Iberian Peninsula\n       </a>\n       in 216\xc2\xa0B.C., they brought the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">\n        Latin language\n       </a>\n       with them, from which all Romance languages descend. The language was spread by Roman soldiers, settlers, and merchants, who built\n       <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">\n        Roman\n       </a>\n       cities mostly near the settlements of previous\n       <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">\n        Celtic\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Celtiberians" title="Celtiberians">\n        Celtiberian\n       </a>\n       civilizations established long before the Roman arrivals.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Between 409 A.D. and 711 A.D., as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">\n        Roman Empire\n       </a>\n       collapsed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">\n        Western Europe\n       </a>\n       , the Iberian Peninsula was conquered by\n       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">\n        Germanic peoples\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">\n        Migration Period\n       </a>\n       . The occupiers, mainly\n       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">\n        Suebi\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">\n        Visigoths\n       </a>\n       who originally spoke\n       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">\n        Germanic languages\n       </a>\n       , quickly adopted late Roman culture and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">\n        Vulgar Latin\n       </a>\n       dialects of the peninsula and over the next 300 years totally integrated into the local populations. After the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">\n        Moorish\n       </a>\n       invasion beginning in 711,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       became the administrative and common language in the conquered regions, but most of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozarabs" title="Mozarabs">\n        remaining Christian population\n       </a>\n       continued to speak a form of\n       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">\n        Romance\n       </a>\n       commonly known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozarabic_language" title="Mozarabic language">\n        Mozarabic\n       </a>\n       , which lasted three centuries longer in\n       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">\n        Spain\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese evolved from the medieval language, known today by linguists as\n       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">\n        Galician-Portuguese\n       </a>\n       , Old Portuguese or Old Galician, of the northwestern medieval\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Kingdom of Galicia">\n        Kingdom of Galicia\n       </a>\n       . It is in Latin administrative documents of the 9th century that written Galician-Portuguese words and phrases are first recorded. This phase is known as Proto-Portuguese, which lasted from the 9th century until the 12th-century independence of the\n       <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">\n        County of Portugal\n       </a>\n       from the Kingdom of Le\xc3\xb3n, by then reigning over Galicia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the first part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">\n        Galician-Portuguese\n       </a>\n       period (from the 12th to the 14th century), the language was increasingly used for documents and other written forms. For some time, it was the language of preference for\n       <a href="/wiki/Lyric_poetry" title="Lyric poetry">\n        lyric poetry\n       </a>\n       in Christian\n       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">\n        Hispania\n       </a>\n       , much as\n       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">\n        Occitan\n       </a>\n       was the language of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_literature#Poetry_of_the_troubadours" title="Occitan literature">\n        poetry of the troubadours\n       </a>\n       in France. Portugal became an independent kingdom in 1139, under King\n       <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Portugal" title="Afonso I of Portugal">\n        Afonso I of Portugal\n       </a>\n       . In 1290, King\n       <a href="/wiki/Denis_of_Portugal" title="Denis of Portugal">\n        Denis of Portugal\n       </a>\n       created the first Portuguese university in Lisbon (the\n       <i>\n        Estudos Gerais\n       </i>\n       , which later moved to\n       <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">\n        Coimbra\n       </a>\n       ) and decreed for Portuguese, then simply called the "common language", to be known as the Portuguese language and used officially.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the second period of Old Portuguese, in the 15th and 16th centuries, with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">\n        Portuguese discoveries\n       </a>\n       , the language was taken to many regions of Africa, Asia, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">\n        Americas\n       </a>\n       . By the mid-16th century, Portuguese had become a\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">\n         lingua franca\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       in Asia and Africa, used not only for colonial administration and trade but also for communication between local officials and Europeans of all nationalities.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Its spread was helped by mixed marriages between Portuguese and local people and by its association with\n       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">\n        Roman Catholic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">\n        missionary\n       </a>\n       efforts, which led to the formation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">\n        creole languages\n       </a>\n       such as that called\n       <a href="/wiki/Kristang_language" title="Kristang language">\n        Kristang\n       </a>\n       in many parts of Asia (from the word\n       <i>\n        crist\xc3\xa3o\n       </i>\n       , "Christian"). The language continued to be popular in parts of Asia until the 19th century. Some Portuguese-speaking Christian communities in\n       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">\n        India\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">\n        Sri Lanka\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">\n        Malaysia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">\n        Indonesia\n       </a>\n       preserved their language even after they were isolated from Portugal.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The end of the Old Portuguese period was marked by the publication of the\n       <i>\n        Cancioneiro Geral\n       </i>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/Garcia_de_Resende" title="Garcia de Resende">\n        Garcia de Resende\n       </a>\n       , in 1516. The early times of Modern Portuguese, which spans the period from the 16th century to the present day, were characterized by an increase in the number of learned words borrowed from\n       <a href="/wiki/Classical_Latin" title="Classical Latin">\n        Classical Latin\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">\n        Classical Greek\n       </a>\n       because of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">\n        Renaissance\n       </a>\n       , which greatly enriched the lexicon. Most literate Portuguese speakers were also literate in Latin; and thus they easily adopted Latin words into their writing\xe2\x80\x94and eventually speech\xe2\x80\x94in Portuguese.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Spanish author\n       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">\n        Miguel de Cervantes\n       </a>\n       once called Portuguese "the sweet and gracious language", while the Brazilian poet\n       <a href="/wiki/Olavo_Bilac" title="Olavo Bilac">\n        Olavo Bilac\n       </a>\n       described it as\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         a \xc3\xbaltima flor do L\xc3\xa1cio, inculta e bela\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("the last flower of\n       <a href="/wiki/Latium" title="Latium">\n        Latium\n       </a>\n       , rustic and beautiful"). Portuguese is also termed "the language of Cam\xc3\xb5es", after\n       <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es" title="Lu\xc3\xads de Cam\xc3\xb5es">\n        Lu\xc3\xads Vaz de Cam\xc3\xb5es\n       </a>\n       , one of the greatest literary figures in the Portuguese language and author of the Portuguese\n       <a href="/wiki/Epic_poetry" title="Epic poetry">\n        epic poem\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Os_Lus%C3%ADadas" title="Os Lus\xc3\xadadas">\n         Os Lus\xc3\xadadas\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In March 2006, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Portuguese_Language" title="Museum of the Portuguese Language">\n        Museum of the Portuguese Language\n       </a>\n       , an interactive museum about the Portuguese language, was founded in\n       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="S\xc3\xa3o Paulo">\n        S\xc3\xa3o Paulo\n       </a>\n       , Brazil, the city with the greatest number of Portuguese language speakers in the world.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOVA_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOVA-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The museum is the first of its kind in the world.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOVA_15-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOVA-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2015 the museum was destroyed in a fire, but there are plans to reconstruct it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution">\n        Geographic distribution\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG/220px-Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG/330px-Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG/440px-Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Multilingual_Emergency_Assembly_Area_Sign_in_Oizumi.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Multilingual sign in Japanese, Portuguese, and English in\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oizumi" title="Oizumi">\n          Oizumi\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n          Japan\n         </a>\n         . Return immigration of\n         <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Brazilians" title="Japanese Brazilians">\n          Japanese Brazilians\n         </a>\n         has led to a large Portuguese-speaking community in the town.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n          <a href="#cite_note-17">\n           [17]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geographic_distribution_of_Portuguese" title="Geographic distribution of Portuguese">\n        Geographic distribution of Portuguese\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese is the native anguage of the vast majority of people in Brazil\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and Portugal,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Special_Eurobarometer_243_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Special_Eurobarometer_243-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and 99.8% of the population of S\xc3\xa3o Tom\xc3\xa9 and Pr\xc3\xadncipe declared speaking Portuguese in the 1991 census.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Perhaps 75% of the population of Angola speaks Portuguese,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and 85% are more or less fluent.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Just over 40% (and rapidly increasing) of the population of Mozambique are native speakers of Portuguese, and 60% are fluent, according to the 2007 census.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Portuguese is also spoken natively by 30% of the population in Guinea-Bissau, and a Portuguese-based creole is understood by all.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       No data is available for Cape Verde, but almost all the population is bilingual, and the monolingual population speaks\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">\n        Cape Verdean Creole\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are also significant Portuguese speaking immigrant communities in many countries including\n       <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">\n        Andorra\n       </a>\n       (15.4%),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">\n        Bermuda\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       (400,275 people in the 2006 census),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">\n        France\n       </a>\n       (900,000 people),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       (400,000 people),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">\n        Jersey\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">\n        Namibia\n       </a>\n       (about 4\xe2\x80\x935% of the population, mainly refugees from Angola in the North of the country),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.namibian.com.na_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-www.namibian.com.na-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">\n        Paraguay\n       </a>\n       (10.7% or 636,000 people),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">\n        Macau\n       </a>\n       (0.6% or 12,000 people),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">\n        Switzerland\n       </a>\n       (196,000 nationals in 2008),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">\n        Venezuela\n       </a>\n       (554,000).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the United States (0.35% of the population or 1,228,126 speakers according to the 2007\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">\n        American Community Survey\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In some parts of former\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">\n        Portuguese India\n       </a>\n       , namely\n       <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">\n        Goa\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">\n        Daman and Diu\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the language is still spoken by about 10,000 people. In 2014, an estimated 1,500 students were learning Portuguese in Goa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Official_status">\n        Official status\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Official status">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_where_Portuguese_is_an_official_language" title="List of countries where Portuguese is an official language">\n        List of countries where Portuguese is an official language\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lusophone_World.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="940" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Lusophone_World.svg/450px-Lusophone_World.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Lusophone_World.svg/675px-Lusophone_World.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Lusophone_World.svg/900px-Lusophone_World.svg.png 2x" width="450"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lusophone_World.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Countries and regions where Portuguese has official status.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">\n        Community of Portuguese Language Countries\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPLP_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CPLP-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (in Portuguese\n       <i>\n        Comunidade dos Pa\xc3\xadses de L\xc3\xadngua Portuguesa\n       </i>\n       , with the Portuguese acronym CPLP) consists of the eight independent countries that have Portuguese as an\n       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">\n        official language\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">\n        Angola\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">\n        Brazil\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">\n        Cape Verde\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">\n        East Timor\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">\n        Equatorial Guinea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">\n        Guinea-Bissau\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">\n        Mozambique\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">\n        Portugal\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="S\xc3\xa3o Tom\xc3\xa9 and Pr\xc3\xadncipe">\n        S\xc3\xa3o Tom\xc3\xa9 and Pr\xc3\xadncipe\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPLP_5-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CPLP-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">\n        Equatorial Guinea\n       </a>\n       made a formal application for full membership to the CPLP in June 2010, a status given only to states with Portuguese as an official language.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2011, Portuguese became its third official language (besides\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       )\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and, in July 2014, the country was accepted as a member of the CPLP.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese is also one of the official languages of the Special Administrative Region of the People\'s Republic of China of Macau (alongside\n       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">\n        Chinese\n       </a>\n       ) and of several international organizations, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">\n        Mercosur\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">\n        Organization of Ibero-American States\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">\n        Union of South American Nations\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">\n        Organization of American States\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">\n        African Union\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africa-union.org_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-africa-union.org-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">\n        Economic Community of West African States\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africa-union.org_46-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-africa-union.org-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">\n        Southern African Development Community\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africa-union.org_46-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-africa-union.org-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">\n        European Union\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population_of_countries_and_jurisdictions_of_Portuguese_official_or_co-official_language">\n        Population of countries and jurisdictions of Portuguese official or co-official language\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       According to\n       <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">\n        The World Factbook\n       </a>\n       country population estimates for 2017, the population of each of the ten jurisdictions is as follows (by descending         <span class="flagicon">\n          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="450" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Flag_of_Macau.svg/23px-Flag_of_Macau.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Flag_of_Macau.svg/35px-Flag_of_Macau.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Flag_of_Macau.svg/45px-Flag_of_Macau.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>\n         </span>\n         <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">\n          Macau\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         644,900\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:left;">\n         <span class="flagicon">\n          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="510" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Cape_Verde.svg/23px-Flag_of_Cape_Verde.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Cape_Verde.svg/35px-Flag_of_Cape_Verde.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Cape_Verde.svg/46px-Flag_of_Cape_Verde.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>\n         </span>\n         <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">\n          Cape Verde\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         560,899\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:left;">\n         <span class="flagicon">\n          <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2800" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sao_Tome_and_Principe.svg.png 1.5x,
