href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="S\xc3\xa3o Tom\xc3\xa9 and Pr\xc3\xadncipe">\n          S\xc3\xa3o Tom\xc3\xa9 and Pr\xc3\xadncipe\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         201,025\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       This means that the population living in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">\n        Lusophone\n       </a>\n       official area is around 280,000,000 inhabitants. This number does not include the Lusophone\n       <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">\n        diaspora\n       </a>\n       , estimated at approximately 10 million people (including 4.5 million Portuguese, 3 million Brazilians, and half a million Cape Verdeans, among others), although it is hard to obtain official accurate numbers of diasporic Portuguese speakers because a significant portion of these citizens are naturalized citizens born outside of Lusophone territory or are children of immigrants, and may have only a basic command of the language. It is also important to note that a large part of the diaspora is a part of the already-counted population of the Portuguese-speaking countries and territories, such as the high number of Brazilian and\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking_African_countries" title="Portuguese-speaking African countries">\n        PALOP\n       </a>\n       emigrant citizens in Portugal or the high number of Portuguese emigrant citizens in the PALOP and Brazil.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Portuguese language therefore serves more than 250 million people daily, who have direct or indirect legal, juridical and social contact with it, varying from the only language used in any contact, to only education, contact with local or international administration, commerce and services or the simple sight of road signs, public information and advertising in Portuguese.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Portuguese_as_a_foreign_language">\n        Portuguese as a foreign language\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Portuguese as a foreign language">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese is a mandatory subject in the school curriculum in\n       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">\n        Uruguay\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">\n        Argentina\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Other countries where Portuguese is taught at schools or is being introduced now include\n       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">\n        Venezuela\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">\n        Zambia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the\n       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">\n        Republic of the Congo\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadao_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-estadao-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">\n        Senegal\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadao_53-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-estadao-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">\n        Namibia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.namibian.com.na_30-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-www.namibian.com.na-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Swaziland" title="Swaziland">\n        Swaziland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadao_53-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-estadao-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">\n        South Africa\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estadao_53-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-estadao-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future">\n        Future\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Future">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       According to estimates by\n       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">\n        UNESCO\n       </a>\n       , Portuguese is the fastest-growing\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_language" title="European language">\n        European language\n       </a>\n       after\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English\n       </a>\n       and the language has, according to the newspaper\n       <i>\n        The Portugal News\n       </i>\n       publishing data given from UNESCO, the highest potential for growth as an international language in\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">\n        southern Africa\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">\n        South America\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Portugal_News_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-The_Portugal_News-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Portuguese is a globalized language spoken officially on five continents, and as a second language by millions worldwide.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since 1991, when Brazil signed into the economic community of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mercosul" title="Mercosul">\n        Mercosul\n       </a>\n       with other South American nations, namely Argentina, Uruguay and Paraguay, Portuguese is either mandatory, or taught, in the schools of those South American countries.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although early in the 21st century, after Macau was ceded to China and Brazilian immigration to Japan slowed down, the use of Portuguese was in decline in Asia, it is once again becoming a language of opportunity there, mostly because of increased diplomatic and financial ties with economically powerful Portuguese-speaking countries (Brazil, Angola, Mozambique, etc.) in the world.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">\n        Dialects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Dialects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_dialects" title="Portuguese dialects">\n        Portuguese dialects\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_in_the_Americas" title="Portuguese in the Americas">\n        Portuguese in the Americas\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1354" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png/220px-Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png/330px-Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png/440px-Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sprachen_Osttimors-en.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Ethnically diverse\n         <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">\n          East Timor\n         </a>\n         has Portuguese as one of its official languages\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         Voc\xc3\xaa\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       is used for educated, formal and colloquial respectful speech in most Portuguese-speaking regions. In the Brazilian state of Rio Grande do Sul,\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         voc\xc3\xaa\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       is virtually absent from the spoken language. In Portugal, it may be considered disrespectful to treat a stranger as\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         voc\xc3\xaa\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       , so the pronoun is either replaced by the name of the person (or a title) or it is omitted, since the verbal conjugation allows the distinction between formal and informal treatment. Riograndense (or Ga\xc3\xbacho) Portuguese normally distinguishes formal from informal speech by verbal conjugation. Informal speech employs\n       <i>\n        tu\n       </i>\n       followed by third person verbs, formal language retains the traditional second person.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Conjugation of\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         tu\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       has three different forms in Brazil (verb "to see":\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         tu viste?\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       , in the traditional second person,\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         tu viu?\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       , in the third person, and\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         tu visse?\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       , in the innovative second person), the conjugation used in the Brazilian states of Par\xc3\xa1, Santa Catarina and Maranh\xc3\xa3o being generally traditional second person, the kind that is used in other Portuguese-speaking countries and learned in Brazilian schools.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The predominance of Southeastern-based media products has established\n       <i>\n        voc\xc3\xaa\n       </i>\n       as the pronoun of choice for the second person singular in both writing and multimedia communications. However, in the city of Rio de Janeiro, the country\'s main cultural centre, the usage of\n       <i>\n        tu\n       </i>\n       has been expanding ever since the end of the 20th century (see,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       a linguistic research on the topic in Portuguese), being most frequent among youngsters and a number of studies have also shown an increase in its use in a number of other Brazilian dialects.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Segunda_pessoa_no_Brasil_II.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="847" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Segunda_pessoa_no_Brasil_II.png/220px-Segunda_pessoa_no_Brasil_II.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Segunda_pessoa_no_Brasil_II.png/330px-Segunda_pessoa_no_Brasil_II.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Segunda_pessoa_no_Brasil_II.png/440px-Segunda_pessoa_no_Brasil_II.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Segunda_pessoa_no_Brasil_II.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The status of second person pronouns in Brazil. Red indicates near exclusive use of\n         <i>\n          voc\xc3\xaa\n         </i>\n         . Mauve indicates decidedly predominant use of\n         <i>\n          tu\n         </i>\n         , but with near exclusive third person (\n         <i>\n          voc\xc3\xaa\n         </i>\n         -like) verbal conjugation. Brown indicates 50-50 tu/voc\xc3\xaa variation, being\n         <i>\n          tu\n         </i>\n         nearly always accompanied by third person (\n         <i>\n          voc\xc3\xaa\n         </i>\n         -like) verbal conjugation. Light blue indicates decidedly predominant to near exclusive use of\n         <i>\n          tu\n         </i>\n         with reasonable frequency of second person (\n         <i>\n          tu\n         </i>\n         -like) verbal conjugation. Yellow indicates balanced voc\xc3\xaa/tu distribution, being\n         <i>\n          tu\n         </i>\n         exclusively accompanied by third person (\n         <i>\n          voc\xc3\xaa\n         </i>\n         -like) verbal conjugation. Green indicates balanced voc\xc3\xaa/tu distribution,\n         <i>\n          tu\n         </i>\n         being predominantly accompanied by third person (\n         <i>\n          voc\xc3\xaa\n         </i>\n         -like) verbal conjugation.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Modern Standard\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Portuguese" title="European Portuguese">\n        European Portuguese\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         portugu\xc3\xaas padr\xc3\xa3o\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       or\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         portugu\xc3\xaas continental\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ) is based on the Portuguese spoken in the area including and surrounding the cities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">\n        Coimbra\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">\n        Lisbon\n       </a>\n       , in central Portugal. Standard European Portuguese is also the preferred standard by the Portuguese-speaking African countries. As such, and despite the fact that its speakers are dispersed around the world, Portuguese has only two dialects used for learning: the European and the Brazilian. Some aspects and sounds found in many dialects of Brazil are exclusive to South America, and cannot be found in Europe. However, the Santomean\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_in_Africa" title="Portuguese in Africa">\n        Portuguese in Africa\n       </a>\n       may be confused with a Brazilian dialect by its phonology and prosody.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Audio samples of some dialects and accents of Portuguese are available below.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are some differences between the areas but these are the best approximations possible. IPA transcriptions refer to the names in local pronunciation.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">\n        Brazil\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Brazil">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ol>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Caipira_dialect" title="Caipira dialect">\n          Caipira\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 Spoken in the states of\n        <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="S\xc3\xa3o Paulo (state)">\n         S\xc3\xa3o Paulo\n        </a>\n        (most markedly on the countryside and rural areas); southern\n        <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">\n         Minas Gerais\n        </a>\n        , northern\n        <a href="/wiki/Paran%C3%A1_(state)" title="Paran\xc3\xa1 (state)">\n         Paran\xc3\xa1\n        </a>\n        and southeastern\n        <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso_do_Sul" title="Mato Grosso do Sul">\n         Mato Grosso do Sul\n        </a>\n        . Depending on the vision of what constitutes\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Tri%C3%A2ngulo_Mineiro" title="Tri\xc3\xa2ngulo Mineiro">\n         Tri\xc3\xa2ngulo Mineiro\n        </a>\n        , border areas of\n        <a href="/wiki/Goi%C3%A1s" title="Goi\xc3\xa1s">\n         Goi\xc3\xa1s\n        </a>\n        and the remaining parts of Mato Grosso do Sul are included, and the frontier of\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        in Minas Gerais is expanded further northerly, though not reaching metropolitan\n        <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">\n         Belo Horizonte\n        </a>\n        . It is often said that\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        appeared by\n        <a href="/wiki/Decreolization" title="Decreolization">\n         decreolization\n        </a>\n        of the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Tupi" title="Old Tupi">\n         l\xc3\xadngua bras\xc3\xadlica\n        </a>\n        and the related\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%ADngua_geral_paulista" title="L\xc3\xadngua geral paulista">\n         l\xc3\xadngua geral paulista\n        </a>\n        , then spoken in almost all of what is now S\xc3\xa3o Paulo, a former\n        <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">\n         lingua franca\n        </a>\n        in most of the contemporary\n        <a href="/wiki/Centro-Sul" title="Centro-Sul">\n         Centro-Sul\n        </a>\n        of Brazil before the 18th century, brought by the\n        <i>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bandeirante" title="Bandeirante">\n          bandeirantes\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        , interior pioneers of\n        <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">\n         Colonial Brazil\n        </a>\n        , closely related to its northern counterpart\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nheengatu_language" title="Nheengatu language">\n         Nheengatu\n        </a>\n        , and that is why the dialect shows many general differences from other variants of the language.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n         <a href="#cite_note-60">\n          [60]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        It has striking remarkable differences in comparison to other Brazilian dialects in phonology, prosody and grammar, often\n        <a href="/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">\n         stigmatized\n        </a>\n        as being strongly associated with a\n        <a href="/wiki/Prestige_(sociolinguistics)" title="Prestige (sociolinguistics)">\n         substandard variant\n        </a>\n        , now mostly rural.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n         <a href="#cite_note-61">\n          [61]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n         <a href="#cite_note-62">\n          [62]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n         <a href="#cite_note-63">\n          [63]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n         <a href="#cite_note-64">\n          [64]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n         <a href="#cite_note-65">\n          [65]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/North_coast_Portuguese" title="North coast Portuguese">\n         <i>\n          Cearense\n         </i>\n         or\n         <i>\n          Costa norte\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 is a dialect spoken more sharply in the states of Cear\xc3\xa1 and Piau\xc3\xad. The variant of Cear\xc3\xa1 includes fairly distinctive traits it shares with the one spoken in Piau\xc3\xad, though, such as distinctive regional phonology and vocabulary (for example, a debuccalization process stronger than that of Portuguese, a different system of the vowel harmony that spans Brazil from\n        <i>\n         fluminense\n        </i>\n        and\n        <i>\n         mineiro\n        </i>\n        to\n        <i>\n         amazofonia\n        </i>\n        but is especially prevalent in\n        <i>\n         nordestino\n        </i>\n        , a very coherent coda sibilant palatalization as those of Portugal and Rio de Janeiro but allowed in fewer environments than in other accents of\n        <i>\n         nordestino\n        </i>\n        , a greater presence of dental stop palatalization to palato-alveolar in comparison to other accents of\n        <i>\n         nordestino\n        </i>\n        , among others, as well as a great number of archaic Portuguese words).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n         <a href="#cite_note-66">\n          [66]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n         <a href="#cite_note-67">\n          [67]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n         <a href="#cite_note-68">\n          [68]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n         <a href="#cite_note-69">\n          [69]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n         <a href="#cite_note-70">\n          [70]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n         <a href="#cite_note-71">\n          [71]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Baiano\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 Found in\n        <a href="/wiki/Bahia" title="Bahia">\n         Bahia\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Sergipe" title="Sergipe">\n         Sergipe\n        </a>\n        , northern Minas Gerais and border regions with\n        <a href="/wiki/Goi%C3%A1s" title="Goi\xc3\xa1s">\n         Goi\xc3\xa1s\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Tocantins" title="Tocantins">\n         Tocantins\n        </a>\n        . Similar to\n        <i>\n         nordestino\n        </i>\n        , it has a very characteristic\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stress_timing" title="Stress timing">\n         syllable-timed rhythm\n        </a>\n        and the greatest tendency to pronounce unstressed vowels as open-mid\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\n         <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">\n          \xc9\x9b\n         </a>\n         ]\n        </span>\n        and\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\n         <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">\n          \xc9\x94\n         </a>\n         ]\n        </span>\n        .\n        <div class="thumb tright">\n         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portugueselanguagedialects-Brazil.png">\n           <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="915" data-file-width="885" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Portugueselanguagedialects-Brazil.png/220px-Portugueselanguagedialects-Brazil.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Portugueselanguagedialects-Brazil.png/330px-Portugueselanguagedialects-Brazil.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Portugueselanguagedialects-Brazil.png/440px-Portugueselanguagedialects-Brazil.png 2x" width="220"/>\n          </a>\n          <div class="thumbcaption">\n           <div class="magnify">\n            <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portugueselanguagedialects-Brazil.png" title="Enlarge">\n            </a>\n           </div>\n           <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">\n            Variants\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/Sociolect" title="Sociolect">\n            sociolects\n           </a>\n           of Brazilian Portuguese.\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">\n         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>\n        </a>\n        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som90.html" rel="nofollow">\n         <i>\n          Fluminense\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 A broad dialect with many variants spoken in the states of\n        <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(state)" title="Rio de Janeiro (state)">\n         Rio de Janeiro\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo" title="Esp\xc3\xadrito Santo">\n         Esp\xc3\xadrito Santo\n        </a>\n        and neighbouring eastern regions of\n        <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">\n         Minas Gerais\n        </a>\n        .\n        <i>\n         Fluminense\n        </i>\n        formed in these previously\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        -speaking areas due to the gradual influence of European migrants, causing many people to distance their speech from their original dialect and incorporate new terms.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n         <a href="#cite_note-72">\n          [72]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <i>\n         Fluminense\n        </i>\n        is sometimes referred to as\n        <i>\n         carioca\n        </i>\n        , however\n        <i>\n         carioca\n        </i>\n        is a more specific term referring to the accent of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Greater Rio de Janeiro">\n         Greater Rio de Janeiro\n        </a>\n        area by speakers with a\n        <i>\n         fluminense\n        </i>\n        dialect.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Ga\xc3\xbacho\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 in\n        <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">\n         Rio Grande do Sul\n        </a>\n        , similar to\n        <i>\n         sulista\n        </i>\n        . There are many distinct accents in Rio Grande do Sul, mainly due to the heavy influx of European immigrants of diverse origins who have settled in colonies throughout the state, and to the proximity to\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanosphere" title="Hispanosphere">\n         Spanish-speaking nations\n        </a>\n        . The\n        <i>\n         ga\xc3\xbacho\n        </i>\n        word in itself is a Spanish\n        <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">\n         loanword\n        </a>\n        into Portuguese of obscure\n        <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">\n         Indigenous Amerindian\n        </a>\n        origins.\n        <div class="thumb tright">\n         <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Falantes_no_mundo.jpg">\n           <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="408" data-file-width="513" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Falantes_no_mundo.jpg/200px-Falantes_no_mundo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Falantes_no_mundo.jpg/300px-Falantes_no_mundo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Falantes_no_mundo.jpg/400px-Falantes_no_mundo.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n          <div class="thumbcaption">\n           <div class="magnify">\n            <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Falantes_no_mundo.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n            </a>\n           </div>\n           Percentage of worldwide Portuguese speakers per country.\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Mineiro" title="Mineiro">\n          Mineiro\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">\n         Minas Gerais\n        </a>\n        (not prevalent in the\n        <a href="/wiki/Tri%C3%A2ngulo_Mineiro" title="Tri\xc3\xa2ngulo Mineiro">\n         Tri\xc3\xa2ngulo Mineiro\n        </a>\n        ). As the\n        <i>\n         fluminense\n        </i>\n        area, its associated region was formerly a sparsely populated land where\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        was spoken, but\n        <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais#History" title="Minas Gerais">\n         the discovery of gold and gems made it the most prosperous Brazilian region\n        </a>\n        , what attracted Portuguese colonists, commoners from other parts of Brazil and their African slaves. South-southwestern,\n        <a href="/wiki/Zona_da_Mata_(Minas_Gerais)" title="Zona da Mata (Minas Gerais)">\n         southeastern\n        </a>\n        and northern areas of the state have fairly distinctive speech, actually approximating to\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         fluminense\n        </i>\n        (popularly called, often pejoratively,\n        <i>\n         carioca do brejo\n        </i>\n        , "marsh carioca") and\n        <i>\n         baiano\n        </i>\n        respectively. Areas including and surrounding\n        <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">\n         Belo Horizonte\n        </a>\n        have a distinctive accent.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">\n         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>\n        </a>\n        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som91.html" rel="nofollow">\n         <i>\n          Nordestino\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_73-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-73">\n          [73]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 more marked in the\n        <a href="/wiki/Sert%C3%A3o" title="Sert\xc3\xa3o">\n         Sert\xc3\xa3o\n        </a>\n        (7), where, in the 19th and 20th centuries and especially in the area including and surrounding the\n        <i>\n         sert\xc3\xa3o\n        </i>\n        (the dry land after\n        <a href="/wiki/Agreste" title="Agreste">\n         Agreste\n        </a>\n        ) of Pernambuco and southern Cear\xc3\xa1, it could sound less comprehensible to speakers of other Portuguese dialects than Galician or\n        <a href="/wiki/Rioplatense_Spanish" title="Rioplatense Spanish">\n         Rioplatense Spanish\n        </a>\n        , and nowadays less distinctive from other variants in the metropolitan cities\n        <a href="/wiki/Zona_da_Mata" title="Zona da Mata">\n         along the coasts\n        </a>\n        . It can be divided in two regional variants, one that includes the northern\n        <a href="/wiki/Maranh%C3%A3o" title="Maranh\xc3\xa3o">\n         Maranh\xc3\xa3o\n        </a>\n        and southern of\n        <a href="/wiki/Piau%C3%AD" title="Piau\xc3\xad">\n         Piau\xc3\xad\n        </a>\n        , and other that goes from\n        <a href="/wiki/Cear%C3%A1" title="Cear\xc3\xa1">\n         Cear\xc3\xa1\n        </a>\n        to\n        <a href="/wiki/Alagoas" title="Alagoas">\n         Alagoas\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Nortista\n        </i>\n        or\n        <i>\n         amazofonia\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 Most of\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" title="Amazon Basin">\n         Amazon Basin\n        </a>\n        states i.e.\n        <a href="/wiki/North_Region,_Brazil" title="North Region, Brazil">\n         Northern Brazil\n        </a>\n        . Before the 20th century, most people from the\n        <i>\n         nordestino\n        </i>\n        area fleeing the droughts and their associated poverty settled here, so it has some similarities with the Portuguese dialect there spoken. The speech in and around the cities of\n        <a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m" title="Bel\xc3\xa9m">\n         Bel\xc3\xa9m\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Manaus" title="Manaus">\n         Manaus\n        </a>\n        has a more European flavor in phonology, prosody and grammar.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Paulistano\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 Variants spoken around\n        <a href="/wiki/Greater_S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="Greater S\xc3\xa3o Paulo">\n         Greater S\xc3\xa3o Paulo\n        </a>\n        in its maximum definition and more easterly areas of S\xc3\xa3o Paulo state, as well perhaps "educated speech" from anywhere in\n        <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="S\xc3\xa3o Paulo (state)">\n         the state of S\xc3\xa3o Paulo\n        </a>\n        (where it coexists with\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        ).\n        <i>\n         Caipira\n        </i>\n        is the hinterland sociolect of much of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Centro-Sul" title="Centro-Sul">\n         Central-Southern half\n        </a>\n        of Brazil, nowadays conservative only in the rural areas and associated with them, that has a historically\n        <a href="/wiki/Prestige_(sociolinguistics)" title="Prestige (sociolinguistics)">\n         low prestige\n        </a>\n        in cities as Rio de Janeiro, Curitiba, Belo Horizonte, and until some years ago, in S\xc3\xa3o Paulo itself.\n        <a href="/wiki/Sociolinguistics" title="Sociolinguistics">\n         Sociolinguistics\n        </a>\n        , or what by times is described as \'\n        <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_discrimination" title="Linguistic discrimination">\n         linguistic prejudice\n        </a>\n        \', often correlated with\n        <a href="/wiki/Class_discrimination" title="Class discrimination">\n         classism\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n         <a href="#cite_note-74">\n          [74]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n         <a href="#cite_note-75">\n          [75]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n         <a href="#cite_note-76">\n          [76]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        is a polemic topic in the entirety of the country since the times of\n        <a href="/wiki/Adoniran_Barbosa#Musical_production" title="Adoniran Barbosa">\n         Adoniran Barbosa\n        </a>\n        . Also, the "Paulistano" accent was heavily influenced by the presence of immigrants in the city of S\xc3\xa3o Paulo, especially the Italians.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Sertanejo\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Center-West_Region,_Brazil" title="Center-West Region, Brazil">\n         Center-Western states\n        </a>\n        , and also much of\n        <a href="/wiki/Tocantins" title="Tocantins">\n         Tocantins\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Rond%C3%B4nia" title="Rond\xc3\xb4nia">\n         Rond\xc3\xb4nia\n        </a>\n        . It is closer to\n        <i>\n         mineiro\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         nordestino\n        </i>\n        or\n        <i>\n         nortista\n        </i>\n        depending on the location.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Sulista\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 The variants spoken in the areas between the northern regions of\n        <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_do_Sul" title="Rio Grande do Sul">\n         Rio Grande do Sul\n        </a>\n        and southern regions of S\xc3\xa3o Paulo state, encompassing most of\n        <a href="/wiki/South_Region,_Brazil" title="South Region, Brazil">\n         southern Brazil\n        </a>\n        . The city of\n        <a href="/wiki/Curitiba" title="Curitiba">\n         Curitiba\n        </a>\n        does have a fairly distinct accent as well, and a relative majority of speakers around and in\n        <a href="/wiki/Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Florian\xc3\xb3polis">\n         Florian\xc3\xb3polis\n        </a>\n        also speak this variant (many speak\n        <i>\n         florianopolitano\n        </i>\n        or\n        <i>\n         manezinho da ilha\n        </i>\n        instead, related to the European Portuguese dialects spoken in\n        <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">\n         Azores\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">\n         Madeira\n        </a>\n        ). Speech of northern Paran\xc3\xa1 is closer to that of inland S\xc3\xa3o Paulo.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Florianopolitan_dialect" title="Florianopolitan dialect">\n          Florianopolitano\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 Variants heavily influenced by European Portuguese spoken in\n        <a href="/wiki/Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Florian\xc3\xb3polis">\n         Florian\xc3\xb3polis\n        </a>\n        city (due to a heavy immigration movement from Portugal, mainly its\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_Portugal" title="Autonomous regions of Portugal">\n         insular regions\n        </a>\n        ) and much of its metropolitan area,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grande_Florian%C3%B3polis" title="Grande Florian\xc3\xb3polis">\n         Grande Florian\xc3\xb3polis\n        </a>\n        , said to be a continuum between those whose speech most resemble\n        <i>\n         sulista\n        </i>\n        dialects and those whose speech most resemble\n        <i>\n         fluminense\n        </i>\n        and European ones, called, often pejoratively,\n        <i>\n         manezinho da ilha\n        </i>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Carioca" title="Carioca">\n          Carioca\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 Not a dialect, but\n        <a href="/wiki/Sociolect" title="Sociolect">\n         sociolects\n        </a>\n        of the\n        <i>\n         fluminense\n        </i>\n        variant spoken in an area roughly corresponding to\n        <a href="/wiki/Greater_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Greater Rio de Janeiro">\n         Greater Rio de Janeiro\n        </a>\n        . It appeared after locals came in contact with the Portuguese aristocracy amidst the\n        <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">\n         Portuguese royal family fled\n        </a>\n        in the early 19th century. There is actually a continuum between Vernacular countryside accents and the\n        <i>\n         carioca\n        </i>\n        sociolect, and the educated speech (in Portuguese\n        <i>\n         norma culta\n        </i>\n        , which most closely resembles other Brazilian Portuguese standards but with marked recent Portuguese influences, the nearest ones among the country\'s dialects along\n        <i>\n         florianopolitano\n        </i>\n        ), so that not all people native to the state of Rio de Janeiro speak the said sociolect, but most\n        <i>\n         carioca\n        </i>\n        speakers will use the standard variant not influenced by it that is rather uniform around Brazil depending on context (emphasis or formality, for example).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Brasiliense\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 used in\n        <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Bras\xc3\xadlia">\n         Bras\xc3\xadlia\n        </a>\n        and its metropolitan area.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n         <a href="#cite_note-77">\n          [77]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        It is not considered a dialect, but more of a regional variant\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 often deemed to be closer to\n        <i>\n         fluminense\n        </i>\n        than the dialect commonly spoken in most of Goi\xc3\xa1s,\n        <i>\n         sertanejo\n        </i>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Arco do desflorestamento\n        </i>\n        or\n        <i>\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dialeto_da_serra_amaz%C3%B4nica" title="pt:Dialeto da serra amaz\xc3\xb4nica">\n          serra amaz\xc3\xb4nica\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 Known in its region as the "accent of the migrants", it has similarities with\n        <i>\n         caipira\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         sertanejo\n        </i>\n        and often\n        <i>\n         sulista\n        </i>\n        that make it differing from\n        <i>\n         amazofonia\n        </i>\n        (in the opposite group of Brazilian dialects, in which it is placed along\n        <i>\n         nordestino\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         baiano\n        </i>\n        ,\n        <i>\n         mineiro\n        </i>\n        and\n        <i>\n         fluminense\n        </i>\n        ). It is the most recent dialect, which appeared by the settlement of families from various other Brazilian regions attracted by the cheap land offer in recently\n        <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">\n         deforested\n        </a>\n        areas.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n         <a href="#cite_note-78">\n          [78]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n         <a href="#cite_note-79">\n          [79]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <i>\n         Recifense\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x80\x94 used in\n        <a href="/wiki/Recife" title="Recife">\n         Recife\n        </a>\n        and its metropolitan area.\n       </li>\n      </ol>\n      <h3>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" </div>\n      </div>\n      <ol>\n       <li>\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">\n         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>\n        </a>\n        <a class="external text" href="http://cvc.instituto-camoes.pt/hlp/geografia/som69.html" rel="nofollow">\n         <i>\n          Micaelense (A\xc3\xa7ores)\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        (S\xc3\xa3o Miguel)\xe2\x80\x94\n        <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">\n         Azores\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loudspeaker.svg">\n         <img alt="Loudspeaker.svg" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png Uruguay\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverense_Portu%C3%B1ol_language" title="Riverense Portu\xc3\xb1ol language">\n         <i>\n          Dialectos Portugueses del Uruguay (DPU)\n         </i>\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Differences between dialects are mostly of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accent_(dialect)" title="Accent (dialect)">\n        accent\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Vocabulary" title="Vocabulary">\n        vocabulary\n       </a>\n       , but between the Brazilian dialects and other dialects, especially in their most colloquial forms, there can also be some grammatical differences. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_creole" title="Portuguese creole">\n        Portuguese-based creoles\n       </a>\n       spoken in various parts of Africa, Asia, and the Americas are independent languages.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Characterization_and_peculiarities">\n        Characterization and peculiarities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Characterization and peculiarities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese, like\n       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">\n        Catalan\n       </a>\n       , preserved the stressed vowels of\n       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">\n        Vulgar Latin\n       </a>\n       , which became diphthongs in most other Romance languages; cf. Port., Cat., Sard.\n       <i>\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pedra" title="wikt:pedra">\n         pedra\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ; Fr.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pierre#French" title="wikt:pierre">\n          pierre\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , Sp.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/piedra#Spanish" title="wikt:piedra">\n          piedra\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , It.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pietra#Italian" title="wikt:pietra">\n          pietra\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , Ro.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="ro" xml:lang="ro">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/piatr%C4%83#Romanian" title="wikt:piatr\xc4\x83">\n          piatr\xc4\x83\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , from Lat.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/petra#Latin" title="wikt:petra">\n          petra\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("stone"); or Port.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fogo#Portuguese" title="wikt:fogo">\n          fogo\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , Cat.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="ca" xml:lang="ca">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/foc#Catalan" title="wikt:foc">\n          foc\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , Sard.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="sc" xml:lang="sc">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fogu#Sardinian" title="wikt:fogu">\n          fogu\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ; Sp.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fuego#Spanish" title="wikt:fuego">\n          fuego\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , It.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="it" xml:lang="it">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fuoco#Italian" title="wikt:fuoco">\n          fuoco\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , Fr.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/feu#French" title="wikt:feu">\n          feu\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , Ro.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="ro" xml:lang="ro">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/foc#Romanian" title="wikt:foc">\n          foc\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , from Lat.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/focus#Latin" title="wikt:focus">\n          focus\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("fire"). Another characteristic of early Portuguese was the loss of\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/intervocalic" title="wiktionary:intervocalic">\n        intervocalic\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        l\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        n\n       </i>\n       , sometimes followed by the merger of the two surrounding vowels, or by the insertion of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Epenthesis" title="Epenthesis">\n        epenthetic vowel\n       </a>\n       between them: cf. Lat.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/salire#Latin" title="wikt:salire">\n          salire\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("to jump"),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tenere#Latin" title="wikt:tenere">\n          tenere\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("to hold"),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/catena#Latin" title="wikt:catena">\n          catena\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("chain"), Sp.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/salir#Spanish" title="wikt:salir">\n          salir\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tener#Spanish" title="wikt:tener">\n          tener\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cadena#Spanish" title="wikt:cadena">\n          cadena\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , Port.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sair#Portuguese" title="wikt:sair">\n          sair\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ter#Portuguese" title="wikt:ter">\n          ter\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cadeia#Portuguese" title="wikt:cadeia">\n          cadeia\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       . This characteristic happens today in\n       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">\n        Celtic languages\n       </a>\n       , such as Irish and Scottish\n       <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">\n        Gaelic\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When the\n       <a href="/wiki/Elision" title="Elision">\n        elided\n       </a>\n       consonant was\n       <i>\n        n\n       </i>\n       , it often\n       <a href="/wiki/Nasalization" title="Nasalization">\n        nasalized\n       </a>\n       the preceding vowel: cf. Lat.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/manum#Latin" title="wikt:manum">\n          manum\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("hand"),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ranam#Latin" title="wikt:ranam">\n          ranam\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("frog"),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/bonum#Latin" title="wikt:bonum">\n          bonum\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("good"), Port.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/m%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:m\xc3\xa3o">\n          m\xc3\xa3o\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/r%C3%A3a#Portuguese" title="wikt:r\xc3\xa3a">\n          r\xc3\xa3a\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/b%C3%B5o#Portuguese" title="wikt:b\xc3\xb5o">\n          b\xc3\xb5o\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (now\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/m%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:m\xc3\xa3o">\n          m\xc3\xa3o\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/r%C3%A3#Portuguese" title="wikt:r\xc3\xa3">\n          r\xc3\xa3\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/bom#Portuguese" title="wikt:bom">\n          bom\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ). This process was the source of most of the language\'s distinctive nasal diphthongs. In particular, the Latin endings\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-anem#Latin" title="wikt:-anem">\n          -anem\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-anum#Latin" title="wikt:-anum">\n          -anum\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-onem#Latin" title="wikt:-onem">\n          -onem\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       became\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:-\xc3\xa3o">\n          -\xc3\xa3o\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       in most cases, cf. Lat.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/canis#Latin" title="wikt:canis">\n          canis\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("dog"),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/germanus#Latin" title="wikt:germanus">\n          germanus\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("brother"),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ratio#Latin" title="wikt:ratio">\n          ratio\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ("reason") with Modern Port.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/c%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:c\xc3\xa3o">\n          c\xc3\xa3o\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/irm%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:irm\xc3\xa3o">\n          irm\xc3\xa3o\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/raz%C3%A3o#Portuguese" title="wikt:raz\xc3\xa3o">\n          raz\xc3\xa3o\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , and their plurals\n       <i>\n        -anes\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        -anos\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        -ones\n       </i>\n       normally became\n       <i>\n        -\xc3\xa3es\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        -\xc3\xa3os\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        -\xc3\xb5es\n       </i>\n       , cf.\n       <i>\n        c\xc3\xa3es\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        irm\xc3\xa3os\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        raz\xc3\xb5es\n       </i>\n       . This nasalisation could be an ancient\n       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Celtic_language" title="Proto-Celtic language">\n        Proto-Celtic\n       </a>\n       characteristic which also exists today in\n       <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">\n        Breton\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaelic_language" title="Gaelic language">\n        Gaelic\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Portuguese language is also the only\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">\n        Romance language\n       </a>\n       that has preserved the clitic case\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mesoclisis" title="Mesoclisis">\n        mesoclisis\n       </a>\n       : cf.\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         dar-te-ei\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (I\'ll give thee),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         amar-te-ei\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (I\'ll love you),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         contact\xc3\xa1-los-ei\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (I\'ll contact them). It was also the only Western Romance language to retain the Latin synthetic\n       <a href="/wiki/Pluperfect" title="Pluperfect">\n        pluperfect\n       </a>\n       tense:\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         eu estivera\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (I had been),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         eu vivera\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (I had lived),\n       <i>\n        <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n         v\xc3\xb3s viv\xc3\xaareis\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       (you had lived)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">\n        Romanian\n       </a>\n       also has this tense, but uses the -s- form.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">\n        Vocabulary\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_vocabulary" title="Portuguese vocabulary">\n        Portuguese vocabulary\n       </a>\n      </div>\n <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="873" data-file-width="768" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg/220px-RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg"
