//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg/440px-RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RealGabinetePortuguesLeitura1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Royal Portuguese Reading Room in\n         <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">\n          Rio de Janeiro\n         </a>\n         , Brazil\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1460" data-file-width="3242" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg/220px-Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg/330px-Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg/440px-Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macau_Museum_Inside.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A sign in the\n         <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Macau" title="Museum of Macau">\n          Museum of Macau\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Most of the lexicon of Portuguese is derived, directly or through other Romance languages, from Latin. Nevertheless, because of its original\n       <a href="/wiki/Celtiberian_language" title="Celtiberian language">\n        Celtiberian\n       </a>\n       heritage and later the participation of Portugal in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">\n        Age of Discovery\n       </a>\n       , it has some\n       <a href="/wiki/Gallaecian_language" title="Gallaecian language">\n        Gallaecian\n       </a>\n       words and adopted\n       <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">\n        loanwords\n       </a>\n       from all over the world.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A number of Portuguese words can still be traced to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">\n        pre-Roman inhabitants of Portugal\n       </a>\n       , which included the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gallaeci" title="Gallaeci">\n        Gallaeci\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">\n        Lusitanians\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">\n        Celtici\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">\n        Cynetes\n       </a>\n       . Most of these words derived from\n       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">\n        Celtic\n       </a>\n       and are very often shared with\n       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">\n        Galician\n       </a>\n       since both languages share a common origin in the medieval language of Galician-Portuguese. A few of these words existed in Latin as loanwords from a\n       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">\n        Celtic\n       </a>\n       source, often\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaulish" title="Gaulish">\n        Gaulish\n       </a>\n       . Altogether these are over 1,000 words, some verbs and toponymic names of towns, rivers, utensils and plants.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 5th century, the Iberian Peninsula (the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">\n        Roman\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">\n        Hispania\n       </a>\n       ) was conquered by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">\n        Germanic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">\n        Suebi\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">\n        Visigoths\n       </a>\n       . As they adopted the Roman civilization and language, however, these people contributed with some 500\n       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">\n        Germanic\n       </a>\n       words to the lexicon. Many of these words are related to warfare\xe2\x80\x94such as\n       <i>\n        espora\n       </i>\n       "spur",\n       <i>\n        estaca\n       </i>\n       "stake", and\n       <i>\n        guerra\n       </i>\n       "war", from\n       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">\n        Gothic\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        *spa\xc3\xbara\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        *stakka\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <i>\n        *wirro\n       </i>\n       , respectively. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">\n        Germanic languages\n       </a>\n       influence also exists in\n       <a href="/wiki/Toponymic_surname" title="Toponymic surname">\n        toponymic surnames\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Patronymic_surname" title="Patronymic surname">\n        patronymic surnames\n       </a>\n       borne by Visigoth sovereigns and their descendants, and it dwells on placenames such has\n       <a href="/wiki/Ermesinde" title="Ermesinde">\n        Ermesinde\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Esposende" title="Esposende">\n        Esposende\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Resende,_Portugal" title="Resende, Portugal">\n        Resende\n       </a>\n       where\n       <i>\n        sinde\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        sende\n       </i>\n       are derived from the Germanic "sinths" (military expedition) and in the case of Resende, the prefix\n       <i>\n        re\n       </i>\n       comes from Germanic "reths" (council). Other examples of Portuguese names, surnames and town names of Germanic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toponymic" title="Toponymic">\n        toponymic\n       </a>\n       origin include Henrique,\n       <a href="/wiki/Henriques_(surname)" title="Henriques (surname)">\n        Henriques\n       </a>\n       , Vermoim, Mandim, Calquim, Baguim, Gemunde, Guetim, Sermonde and many more, are quite common mainly in the old\n       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">\n        Suebi\n       </a>\n       and later\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visigothic" title="Visigothic">\n        Visigothic\n       </a>\n       dominated regions, covering today\'s Northern half of Portugal and\n       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">\n        Galicia\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Between the 9th and early 13th centuries, Portuguese acquired nearly 800 words from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       by influence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">\n        Moorish Iberia\n       </a>\n       . They are often recognizable by the initial\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Definite_article_in_Arabic" title="Definite article in Arabic">\n        Arabic article\n        <i>\n         a(l)-\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , and include many common words such as\n       <i>\n        aldeia\n       </i>\n       "village" from \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb6\xd9\x8a\xd8\xb9\xd8\xa9\n       <i>\n        al\xe1\xb8\x8dai`a\n       </i>\n       (or from\n       <a href="/wiki/Edictum_Rothari" title="Edictum Rothari">\n        Edictum Rothari\n       </a>\n       :\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Aldii" title="Aldii">\n         aldii\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        aldias\n       </i>\n       ),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        alface\n       </i>\n       "lettuce" from \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xae\xd8\xb3\n       <i>\n        alkhass\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        armaz\xc3\xa9m\n       </i>\n       "warehouse" from \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd9\x85\xd8\xae\xd8\xb2\xd9\x86\n       <i>\n        almakhzan\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <i>\n        azeite\n       </i>\n       "olive oil" from \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xb2\xd9\x8a\xd8\xaa\n       <i>\n        azzait\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Starting in the 15th century, the Portuguese maritime explorations led to the introduction of many loanwords from Asian languages. For instance,\n       <i>\n        catana\n       </i>\n       "cutlass" from\n       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">\n        Japanese\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        katana\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        ch\xc3\xa1\n       </i>\n       "tea" from\n       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">\n        Chinese\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Tea#Etymology" title="Tea">\n         <i>\n          ch\xc3\xa1\n         </i>\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From the 16th to the 19th centuries, because of the role of Portugal as intermediary in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">\n        Atlantic slave trade\n       </a>\n       , and the establishment of large Portuguese colonies in Angola, Mozambique, and Brazil, Portuguese acquired several words of African and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples of Brazil">\n        Amerind\n       </a>\n       origin, especially names for most of the animals and plants found in those territories. While those terms are mostly used in the former colonies, many became current in European Portuguese as well. From\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kimbundu_language" title="Kimbundu language">\n        Kimbundu\n       </a>\n       , for example, came\n       <i>\n        kifumate\n       </i>\n       &gt;\n       <i>\n        cafun\xc3\xa9\n       </i>\n       "head caress" (Brazil),\n       <i>\n        kusula\n       </i>\n       &gt;\n       <i>\n        ca\xc3\xa7ula\n       </i>\n       "youngest child" (Brazil),\n       <i>\n        marimbondo\n       </i>\n       "tropical wasp" (Brazil), and\n       <i>\n        kubungula\n       </i>\n       &gt;\n       <i>\n        bungular\n       </i>\n       "to dance like a wizard" (Angola). From South America came\n       <i>\n        batata\n       </i>\n       "\n       <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">\n        potato\n       </a>\n       ", from\n       <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_language" title="Ta\xc3\xadno language">\n        Taino\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <i>\n        anan\xc3\xa1s\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        abacaxi\n       </i>\n       , from\n       <a href="/wiki/Tupi%E2%80%93Guarani_languages" title="Tupi\xe2\x80\x93Guarani languages">\n        Tupi\xe2\x80\x93Guarani\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        nan\xc3\xa1\n       </i>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tupi_language" title="Tupi language">\n        Tupi\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        ib\xc3\xa1 cati\n       </i>\n       , respectively (two species of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">\n        pineapple\n       </a>\n       ), and\n       <i>\n        pipoca\n       </i>\n       "\n       <a href="/wiki/Popcorn" title="Popcorn">\n        popcorn\n       </a>\n       " from\n       <a href="/wiki/Tupi_language" title="Tupi language">\n        Tupi\n       </a>\n       and\n       <i>\n        tucano\n       </i>\n       "\n       <a href="/wiki/Toucan" title="Toucan">\n        toucan\n       </a>\n       " from\n       <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">\n        Guarani\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        tucan\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Finally, it has received a steady influx of loanwords from other European languages, especially French and\n       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">\n        English\n       </a>\n       . These are by far the most important languages when referring to loanwords. There are many examples such as:\n       <i>\n        colchete\n       </i>\n       /\n       <i>\n        croch\xc3\xaa\n       </i>\n       "bracket"/"crochet",\n       <i>\n        palet\xc3\xb3\n       </i>\n       "jacket",\n       <i>\n        batom\n       </i>\n       "lipstick", and\n       <i>\n        fil\xc3\xa9\n       </i>\n       /\n       <i>\n        filete\n       </i>\n       "steak"/"slice",\n       <i>\n        rua\n       </i>\n       "street" respectively, from French\n       <i>\n        crochet\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        paletot\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        b\xc3\xa2ton\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        filet\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        rue\n       </i>\n       ; and\n       <i>\n        bife\n       </i>\n       "steak",\n       <i>\n        futebol\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        rev\xc3\xb3lver\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        stock\n       </i>\n       /\n       <i>\n        estoque\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        folclore\n       </i>\n       , from English\n       <i>\n        beef\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        football\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        revolver\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        stock\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        folklore\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Examples from other European languages:\n       <i>\n        macarr\xc3\xa3o\n       </i>\n       "pasta",\n       <i>\n        piloto\n       </i>\n       "pilot",\n       <i>\n        carro\xc3\xa7a\n       </i>\n       "carriage", and\n       <i>\n        barraca\n       </i>\n       "barrack", from Italian\n       <i>\n        maccherone\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        pilota\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        carrozza\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <i>\n        baracca\n       </i>\n       ;\n       <i>\n        melena\n       </i>\n       "hair lock",\n       <i>\n        fiambre\n       </i>\n       "wet-cured ham" (in Portugal, in contrast with\n       <i>\n        presunto\n       </i>\n       "dry-cured ham" from Latin\n       <i>\n        prae-exsuctus\n       </i>\n       "dehydrated") or "canned ham" (in Brazil, in contrast with non-canned, wet-cured\n       <i>\n        presunto cozido\n       </i>\n       and dry-cured\n       <i>\n        presunto cru\n       </i>\n       ), and\n       <i>\n        castelhano\n       </i>\n       "Castilian", from Spanish\n       <i>\n        melena\n       </i>\n       "mane",\n       <i>\n        fiambre\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        castellano\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Before the last four decades, Brazilians adopted a greater number of loanwords from Japanese and other European languages (due to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Brazil" title="Immigration to Brazil">\n        historical immigration\n       </a>\n       affecting their demographics), and they were and are also more willing to adopt foreign terms that come from\n       <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">\n        globalization\n       </a>\n       than the Portuguese, while the degree of African, Tupian and other Amerindian lexicon in Brazilian Portuguese is shown to be surprisingly lesser than that commonly expected of the said variant by the local Africanist and Indianist academia (that also has to some degree influenced the common sense of what gives a different cultural identity of Brazilians in relation to the Portuguese), so that its lexicon is almost identical (about 99%) to that of European Portuguese.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dummies_85-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dummies-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Many Portuguese settlers to Colonial Brazil were from northern and insular Portugal,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       apart from some historically important\n       <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration" title="Illegal immigration">\n        illegal immigrants\n       </a>\n       from elsewhere in Europe, such as Galicia, France and the Netherlands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n        <a href="#cite_note-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It should be noted that Brazil received more European immigrants in its colonial history than the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       . Between 1500 and 1760, 700,000 Europeans (overwhelmingly Portuguese) settled in Brazil, while 530,000 Europeans settled in the United States for the same given time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_89-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification_and_related_languages">\n        Classification and related languages\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Classification and related languages">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="600" height="326" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/360px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/540px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 2x" width="360"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map showing the historical retreat and expansion of Portuguese (\n         <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">\n          Galician-Portuguese\n         </a>\n         ) within the context of its linguistic neighbours between the year 1000 and 2000.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="820" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG/320px-Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG/480px-Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG/640px-Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG 2x" width="320"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lenguas_y_dialectos_iberorromances.PNG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map showing mostly contemporary\n         <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">\n          West Iberian\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a href="/wiki/Occitano-Romance_languages" title="Occitano-Romance languages">\n          Occitano-Romance\n         </a>\n         languages, as well many of their mainland European dialects (take note that areas colored green,\n         <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language" title="Aragonese language">\n          gold\n         </a>\n         or pink/purple represent languages deemed\n         <a href="/wiki/Endangered_language" title="Endangered language">\n          endangered\n         </a>\n         by UNESCO, so this may be outdated in less than a few decades). It shows European Portuguese,\n         <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">\n          Galician\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Galician-Asturian" title="Galician-Asturian">\n          Eonavian\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">\n          Mirandese\n         </a>\n         and the\n         <a href="/wiki/Fala_language" title="Fala language">\n          Fala\n         </a>\n         as not only closely related but as\n         <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">\n          dialect continuum\n         </a>\n         , though it excludes dialects spoken in insular Portugal (Azores and Madeira\xe2\x80\x93\n         <a href="/wiki/Canarian_Spanish" title="Canarian Spanish">\n          Canaries\n         </a>\n         is not shown either).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">\n        Iberian Romance languages\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">\n        Galician-Portuguese\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comparison_of_Spanish_and_Portuguese" title="Comparison of Spanish and Portuguese">\n        Comparison of Spanish and Portuguese\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese belongs to the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">\n        West Iberian\n       </a>\n       branch of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">\n        Romance languages\n       </a>\n       , and it has special ties with the following members of this group:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">\n         Galician\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Fala_language" title="Fala language">\n         Fala\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverense_Portu%C3%B1ol_language" title="Riverense Portu\xc3\xb1ol language">\n         <i>\n          portunhol do pampa\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        (the way\n        <i>\n         riverense\n        </i>\n        and its sibling dialects are referred to in Portuguese), its closest relatives.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">\n         Mirandese\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leonese_language" title="Leonese language">\n         Leonese\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">\n         Asturian\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Extremaduran_language" title="Extremaduran language">\n         Extremaduran\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_dialect" title="Cantabrian dialect">\n         Cantabrian\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese_languages" title="Astur-Leonese languages">\n         Astur-Leonese languages\n        </a>\n        ). Mirandese is the only recognised regional language spoken in Portugal (beside Portuguese, the only official language in Portugal).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n         Spanish\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Cal%C3%B3_language" title="Cal\xc3\xb3 language">\n         <i>\n          cal\xc3\xa3o\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        (the way\n        <i>\n         cal\xc3\xb3\n        </i>\n        , language of the Iberian\n        <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">\n         Romani\n        </a>\n        , is referred to in Portuguese).\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese and other Romance languages (namely French and Italian) are not mutually intelligible, although they share considerable similarities in both vocabulary and grammar. Portuguese speakers will usually need some formal study before attaining strong comprehension in those Romance languages, and vice versa. However, Portuguese and Galician are mutually intelligible. Given that Portuguese has a larger phonemic inventory than Spanish, Portuguese is only moderately intelligible to some Spanish speakers, despite the strong lexical and grammatical similarity (89%) between the two.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Portu%C3%B1ol" title="Portu\xc3\xb1ol">\n        <i>\n         Portunhol\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       , a form of\n       <a href="/wiki/Code-switching" title="Code-switching">\n        code-switching\n       </a>\n       , has a more lively use and is more readily mentioned in popular culture in South America. Said code-switching is not to be confused with the\n       <i>\n        portunhol\n       </i>\n       spoken on the borders of Brazil with Uruguay (\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         dialeto do pampa\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ) and Paraguay (\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         dialeto dos\n         <a href="/wiki/Brasiguayos" title="Brasiguayos">\n          brasiguaios\n         </a>\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ), and of Portugal with Spain (\n       <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Barranquenho" title="Barranquenho">\n          barranquenho\n         </a>\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ), that are Portuguese dialects spoken natively by thousands of people, which have been heavily influenced by Spanish.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipski_94-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipski-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese and Spanish are the only Ibero-Romance languages, and perhaps the only Romance languages with such thriving inter-language forms, in which visible and lively bilingual contact dialects and code-switching have formed, in which functional bilingual communication is achieved through attempting an approximation to the target foreign language (known as \'Portunhol\') without a learned acquisition process, but nevertheless facilitates communication. There is an emerging literature focused on such phenomena (including informal attempts of standardization of the linguistic continua and their usage).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lipski_94-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lipski-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Galician-Portuguese_in_Spain">\n        Galician-Portuguese in Spain\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Galician-Portuguese in Spain">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Reintegrationism" title="Reintegrationism">\n        Reintegrationism\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The closest relative of Portuguese is Galician, which is spoken in the autonomous community (region) of\n       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">\n        Galicia\n       </a>\n       (northwestern Spain). The two were at one time a single language, known today as\n       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">\n        Galician-Portuguese\n       </a>\n       , but they have diverged especially in pronunciation and vocabulary due to the political separation of Portugal from Galicia. There is, however, still a linguistic continuity consisting of the variant of Galician referred to as\n       <i>\n        galego-portugu\xc3\xaas baixo-limiao\n       </i>\n       , which is spoken in several Galician villages between the municipalities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Entrimo" title="Entrimo">\n        Entrimo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lobios" title="Lobios">\n        Lobios\n       </a>\n       and the transborder region of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Peneda-Ger%C3%AAs_National_Park" title="Peneda-Ger\xc3\xaas National Park">\n        natural park of Peneda-Ger\xc3\xaas/Xur\xc3\xaas\n       </a>\n       . It is "considered a rarity, a living vestige of the medieval language that ranged from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">\n        Cantabria\n       </a>\n       to\n       <a href="/wiki/Mondego_River" title="Mondego River">\n        Mondego\n       </a>\n       [...]".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agal-gz.or_95-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-agal-gz.or-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As reported by UNESCO, due to the pressure of the Spanish language on the standard official version of the Galician language, the Galician language was on the verge of disappearing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agal-gz.or_95-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-agal-gz.or-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to the Unesco philologist Tapani Salminen, the proximity to Portuguese protects Galician.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Nevertheless, the core vocabulary and grammar of Galician are still noticeably closer to Portuguese than to those of Spanish. In particular, like Portuguese, it uses the future subjunctive, the personal infinitive, and the synthetic pluperfect. Mutual intelligibility (estimated at 90% by R. A. Hall, Jr., 1989)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is excellent between Galicians and northern Portuguese. Many linguists consider\n       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">\n        Galician\n       </a>\n       to be a co-dialect of the Portuguese language.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another member of the Galician-Portuguese group, most commonly thought of as a Galician dialect, is spoken in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Asturian" title="Galician-Asturian">\n        Eonavian\n       </a>\n       region in a western strip in\n       <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">\n        Asturias\n       </a>\n       and the westernmost parts of the provinces of\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Province of Le\xc3\xb3n">\n        Le\xc3\xb3n\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Zamora" title="Province of Zamora">\n        Zamora\n       </a>\n       , along the frontier with Galicia, between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eo_(river)" title="Eo (river)">\n        Eo\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Navia_(river)" title="Navia (river)">\n        Navia\n       </a>\n       rivers (or more exactly Eo and Frexulfe rivers). It is called\n       <i>\n        eonaviego\n       </i>\n       or\n       <i>\n        gallego-asturiano\n       </i>\n       by its speakers.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Fala language, known by its speakers as\n       <i>\n        xalim\xc3\xa9s\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        ma\xc3\xb1egu\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        a fala de X\xc3\xa1lima\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        chapurr\xc3\xa1u\n       </i>\n       and in Portuguese as\n       <i>\n        a fala de X\xc3\xa1lima\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        a fala da Estremadura\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        o galego da Estremadura\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        valego\n       </i>\n       ou\n       <i>\n        galaico-estremenho\n       </i>\n       , is another descendant of Galician-Portuguese, spoken by a small number of people in the Spanish towns of\n       <a href="/wiki/Valverde_del_Fresno" title="Valverde del Fresno">\n        Valverde del Fresno\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Valverdi du Fresnu\n       </i>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Eljas" title="Eljas">\n        Eljas\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        As Ellas\n       </i>\n       ) and\n       <a href="/wiki/San_Mart%C3%ADn_de_Trevejo" title="San Mart\xc3\xadn de Trevejo">\n        San Mart\xc3\xadn de Trevejo\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Sa Mart\xc3\xadn de Trevellu\n       </i>\n       ) in the autonomous community of\n       <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">\n        Extremadura\n       </a>\n       , near the border with Portugal.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There are a number of other places in Spain in which the native language of the common people is a descendant of the Galician-Portuguese group, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/La_Alamedilla" title="La Alamedilla">\n        La Alamedilla\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cedillo" title="Cedillo">\n        Cedillo\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Cedilho\n       </i>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Herrera_de_Alc%C3%A1ntara" title="Herrera de Alc\xc3\xa1ntara">\n        Herrera de Alc\xc3\xa1ntara\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Ferreira d\'Alc\xc3\xa2ntara\n       </i>\n       ) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Olivenza" title="Olivenza">\n        Olivenza\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Oliven\xc3\xa7a\n       </i>\n       ), but in these municipalities, what is spoken is actually Portuguese, not disputed as such in the mainstream.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It should be noticed that the diversity of dialects of the Portuguese language is known since the time of medieval Portuguese-Galician language when it coexisted with the Lusitanian-Mozarabic dialect, spoken in the south of Portugal. The dialectal diversity becomes more evident in the work of\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fern%C3%A3o_d%27Oliveira&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fern\xc3\xa3o d\'Oliveira (page does not exist)">\n        Fern\xc3\xa3o d\'Oliveira\n       </a>\n       , in the\n       <b>\n        Grammatica da Lingoagem Portuguesa\n       </b>\n       , (1536), where he remarks that the people of Portuguese regions of Beira, Alentejo, Estremadura, and Entre Douro e Minho, all speak differently from each other. Also\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Contador_d%27Argote&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Contador d\'Argote (page does not exist)">\n        Contador d\'Argote\n       </a>\n       (1725) distinguishes three main varieties of dialects: the local dialects, the dialects of time, and of profession (work jargon). Of local dialects he highlights five main dialects: the dialect of Estremadura, of Entre-Douro e Minho, of Beira, of Algarve and of Tr\xc3\xa1s-os-Montes. He also makes reference to the overseas dialects, the rustic dialects, the poetic dialect and that of prose.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the kingdom of Portugal,\n       <i>\n        Ladinho\n       </i>\n       (or\n       <i>\n        Lingoagem Ladinha\n       </i>\n       ) was the name given to the pure Portuguese language romance, without any mixture of Aravia or Gerigon\xc3\xa7a Judenga.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While the term\n       <i>\n        l\xc3\xadngua vulgar\n       </i>\n       was used to name the language before D. Dinis decided to call it "Portuguese language",\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the erudite version used and known as Galician-Portuguese (the language of the Portuguese court) and all other Portuguese dialects were spoken at the same time. In a historical perspective the Portuguese language was never just one dialect. Just like today there is a standard Portuguese (actually two) among the several dialects of Portuguese, in the past there was Galician-Portuguese as the "standard", coexisting with other dialects.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_on_other_languages">\n        Influence on other languages\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Influence on other languages">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_words_of_Portuguese_origin" title="List of English words of Portuguese origin">\n        List of English words of Portuguese origin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loan_words_in_Malayalam#Portuguese" title="Loan words in Malayalam">\n        Loan words in Malayalam \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Portuguese\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loan_words_in_Indonesian" title="Loan words in Indonesian">\n        Loan words in Indonesian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_words_of_Portuguese_origin" title="Japanese words of Portuguese origin">\n        Japanese words of Portuguese origin\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Malay_loanwords" title="List of Malay loanwords">\n        List of Malay loanwords\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_loanwords_in_Sinhala" title="Portuguese loanwords in Sinhala">\n        Portuguese loanwords in Sinhala\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loan_words_in_Sri_Lankan_Tamil#Portuguese" title="Loan words in Sri Lankan Tamil">\n        Loan words in Sri Lankan Tamil \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Portuguese\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Indo-Portuguese_language" title="Sri Lanka Indo-Portuguese language">\n        Sri Lanka Indo-Portuguese language\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese has provided\n       <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">\n        loanwords\n       </a>\n       to many languages, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">\n        Indonesian\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Manado_Malay" title="Manado Malay">\n        Manado Malay\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">\n        Malayalam\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Tamils_(native)" title="Sri Lanka Tamils (native)">\n        Sri Lankan Tamil\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_language" title="Sinhalese language">\n        Sinhalese\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">\n        Malay\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">\n        Bengali\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_(language)" title="English (language)">\n        English\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">\n        Hindi\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">\n        Swahili\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">\n        Afrikaans\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Konkani_language" title="Konkani language">\n        Konkani\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Marathi_language" title="Marathi language">\n        Marathi\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tetum_language" title="Tetum language">\n        Tetum\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsonga_language" title="Tsonga language">\n        Xitsonga\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">\n        Japanese\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Lanc-Patu%C3%A1_creole" title="Lanc-Patu\xc3\xa1 creole">\n        Lanc-Patu\xc3\xa1\n       </a>\n       (spoken in northern Brazil),\n       <a href="/wiki/Esan_people#Language" title="Esan people">\n        Esan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sranan_Tongo" title="Sranan Tongo">\n        Sranan Tongo\n       </a>\n       (spoken in Suriname). It left a strong influence on the\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Tupi" title="Old Tupi">\n         l\xc3\xadngua bras\xc3\xadlica\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tupi%E2%80%93Guarani_language" title="Tupi\xe2\x80\x93Guarani language">\n        Tupi\xe2\x80\x93Guarani language\n       </a>\n       , which was the most widely spoken in Brazil until the 18th century, and on the language spoken around\n       <a href="/wiki/Sikka_Regency" title="Sikka Regency">\n        Sikka\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">\n        Flores\n       </a>\n       Island,\n       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">\n        Indonesia\n       </a>\n       . In nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Larantuka" title="Larantuka">\n        Larantuka\n       </a>\n       , Portuguese is used for prayers in\n       <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week" title="Holy Week">\n        Holy Week\n       </a>\n       rituals. The Japanese\xe2\x80\x93Portuguese dictionary\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Nippo_Jisho" title="Nippo Jisho">\n         Nippo Jisho\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (1603) was the first dictionary of Japanese in a European language, a product of\n       <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">\n        Jesuit\n       </a>\n       missionary activity in Japan. Building on the work of earlier Portuguese missionaries, the\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dictionarium_Anamiticum,_Lusitanum_et_Latinum" title="Dictionarium Anamiticum, Lusitanum et Latinum">\n         Dictionarium Anamiticum, Lusitanum et Latinum\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (Annamite\xe2\x80\x93Portuguese\xe2\x80\x93Latin dictionary) of\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_de_Rhodes" title="Alexandre de Rhodes">\n        Alexandre de Rhodes\n       </a>\n       (1651) introduced the modern\n       <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_alphabet" title="Vietnamese alphabet">\n        orthography of Vietnamese\n       </a>\n       , which is based on the orthography of 17th-century Portuguese. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Romanization" title="Romanization">\n        Romanization\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">\n        Chinese\n       </a>\n       was also influenced by the Portuguese language (among others), particularly regarding\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_common_Chinese_surnames" title="List of common Chinese surnames">\n        Chinese surnames\n       </a>\n       ; one example is\n       <i>\n        Mei\n       </i>\n       . During 1583\xe2\x80\x9388\n       <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">\n        Italian\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuits" title="Jesuits">\n        Jesuits\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Michele_Ruggieri" title="Michele Ruggieri">\n        Michele Ruggieri\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Ricci" title="Matteo Ricci">\n        Matteo Ricci\n       </a>\n       created a Portuguese\xe2\x80\x93Chinese dictionary\xe2\x80\x94the first ever European\xe2\x80\x93Chinese dictionary.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-camus_101-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-camus-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ricciDict_102-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ricciDict-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For instance, as\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">\n        Portuguese merchants\n       </a>\n       were presumably the first to introduce the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_orange" title="Sweet orange">\n        sweet orange\n       </a>\n       in Europe, in several modern\n       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">\n        Indo-European languages\n       </a>\n       the fruit has been named after them. Some examples are Albanian\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portokall#Albanian" title="wikt:portokall">\n        portokall\n       </a>\n       , Bulgarian\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%BB#Bulgarian" title="wikt:\xd0\xbf\xd0\xbe\xd1\x80\xd1\x82\xd0\xbe\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbb">\n        \xd0\xbf\xd0\xbe\xd1\x80\xd1\x82\xd0\xbe\xd0\xba\xd0\xb0\xd0\xbb\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        portokal\n       </i>\n       ), Greek\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CF%80%CE%BF%CF%81%CF%84%CE%BF%CE%BA%CE%AC%CE%BB%CE%B9#Greek" title="wikt:\xcf\x80\xce\xbf\xcf\x81\xcf\x84\xce\xbf\xce\xba\xce\xac\xce\xbb\xce\xb9">\n        \xcf\x80\xce\xbf\xcf\x81\xcf\x84\xce\xbf\xce\xba\xce\xac\xce\xbb\xce\xb9\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        portokali\n       </i>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_language" title="Macedonian language">\n        Macedonian\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Macedonian transliteration">\n         portokal\n        </span>\n       </i>\n       , Persian\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D9%BE%D8%B1%D8%AA%D9%82%D8%A7%D9%84#Persian" title="wikt:\xd9\xbe\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaa\xd9\x82\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84">\n        \xd9\xbe\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaa\xd9\x82\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        porteghal\n       </i>\n       ), and Romanian\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portocal%C4%83#Romanian" title="wikt:portocal\xc4\x83">\n        portocal\xc4\x83\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plantname_103-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-plantname-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OstergrenBosse2011_104-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OstergrenBosse2011-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Related names can be found in other languages, such as Arabic\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A8%D8%B1%D8%AA%D9%82%D8%A7%D9%84#Arabic" title="wikt:\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaa\xd9\x82\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84">\n        \xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\xd8\xa8\xd8\xb1\xd8\xaa\xd9\x82\xd8\xa7\xd9\x84\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        bourtouqal\n       </i>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">\n        Georgian\n       </a>\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%83%A4%E1%83%9D%E1%83%A0%E1%83%97%E1%83%9D%E1%83%AE%E1%83%90%E1%83%9A%E1%83%98#Georgian" title="wikt:\xe1\x83\xa4\xe1\x83\x9d\xe1\x83\xa0\xe1\x83\x97\xe1\x83\x9d\xe1\x83\xae\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\x9a\xe1\x83\x98">\n        \xe1\x83\xa4\xe1\x83\x9d\xe1\x83\xa0\xe1\x83\x97\xe1\x83\x9d\xe1\x83\xae\xe1\x83\x90\xe1\x83\x9a\xe1\x83\x98\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        p\'ort\'oxali\n       </i>\n       ), Turkish\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portakal#Turkish" title="wikt:portakal">\n        portakal\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Amharic" title="Amharic">\n        Amharic\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        birtukan\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plantname_103-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-plantname-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Also, in\n       <a href="/wiki/Regional_Italian" title="Regional Italian">\n        southern Italian dialects\n       </a>\n       (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/Neapolitan_language" title="Neapolitan language">\n        Neapolitan\n       </a>\n       ), an orange is\n       <i>\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/portogallo" title="wikt:portogallo">\n         portogallo\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       or\n       <i>\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/it:purtuallo" title="wikt:it:purtuallo">\n         purtuallo\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , literally "(the) Portuguese (one)", in contrast to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Italian" title="Standard Italian">\n        standard Italian\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        arancia\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Derived_languages">\n        Derived languages\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Derived languages">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-based_creole_languages" title="Portuguese-based creole languages">\n        Portuguese-based creole languages\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Beginning in the 16th century, the extensive contacts between Portuguese travelers and settlers, African and Asian slaves, and local populations led to the appearance of many\n       <a href="/wiki/Pidgin" title="Pidgin">\n        pidgins\n       </a>\n       with varying amounts of Portuguese influence. As each of these pidgins became the mother tongue of succeeding generations, they evolved into fully fledged\n       <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">\n        creole languages\n       </a>\n       , which remained in use in many parts of Asia, Africa and South America until the 18th century. Some Portuguese-based or Portuguese-influenced creoles are still spoken today, by over 3 million people worldwide, especially people of partial\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       ancestry.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">\n        Phonology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Phonology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_phonology" title="Portuguese phonology">\n        Portuguese phonology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese phonology is similar to those of languages such as\n       <a href="/wiki/French_phonology" title="French phonology">\n        French\n       </a>\n       (especially\n       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_French_phonology" title="Quebec French phonology">\n        that of Quebec\n       </a>\n       ), the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Italic_languages" title="Gallo-Italic languages">\n        Gallo-Italic languages\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_phonology" title="Occitan phonology">\n        Occitan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_phonology" title="Catalan phonology">\n        Catalan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Franco-Proven%C3%A7al_language" title="Franco-Proven\xc3\xa7al language">\n        Franco-Proven\xc3\xa7al\n       </a>\n       , unlike\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology" title="Spanish phonology">\n        that of Spanish\n       </a>\n       , which is similar to those of\n       <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">\n        Sardinian\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Neapolitan_language" title="Neapolitan language">\n        Southern Italian dialects\n       </a>\n       . Some would describe the phonology of Portuguese as a blend of\n       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">\n        Spanish\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">\n        Gallo-Romance\n       </a>\n       (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       ) and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Italic_languages" title="Gallo-Italic languages">\n        languages of northern Italy\n       </a>\n       (especially\n       <a href="/wiki/Genoese_dialect" title="Genoese dialect">\n        Genoese\n       </a>\n       ), but with a deeper\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celtic_language" title="Celtic language">\n        Celtic\n       </a>\n       influence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is a maximum of 9 oral vowels, 2 semivowels and 21 consonants; though some varieties of the language have fewer phonemes. There are also five\n       <a href="/wiki/Nasal_vowel" title="Nasal vowel">\n        nasal vowels\n       </a>\n       , which some linguists regard as allophones of the oral vowels.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">\n        Vowels\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Vowels">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="980" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg/250px-European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg/375px-European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg/500px-European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Portuguese_vowel_chart.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Chart of monophthongs of the Portuguese of Lisbon, with its\n         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n          /\xc9\x90, \xc9\x90\xcc\x83/\n         </span>\n         in central\n         <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">\n          schwa\n         </a>\n         position.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Like\n       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">\n        Catalan\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">\n        German\n       </a>\n       , Portuguese uses vowel quality to contrast stressed syllables with unstressed syllables: isolated vowels tend to be\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vowel_height" title="Vowel height">\n        raised\n       </a>\n       , and in some cases centralized, when unstressed.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">\n       <a href="/wiki/Flap_consonant" title="Flap consonant">\n           flap\n          </a>\n         </small>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="IPA" </span>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Phonetic notes\n       </b>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Semivowels contrast with unstressed high vowels in verbal conjugation, as in\n        <i>\n         (eu) rio\n        </i>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /\xcb\x88\xca\x81i.u/\n        </span>\n        and\n        <i>\n         (ele) riu\n        </i>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /\xcb\x88\xca\x81iw/\n        </span>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n         <a href="#cite_note-110">\n          [110]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Phonologists discuss whether their nature is vowel or consonant.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n         <a href="#cite_note-111">\n          [111]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        In most of Brazil and Angola, the consonant hereafter denoted as\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /\xc9\xb2/\n        </span>\n        is realized as a\n        <a href="/wiki/Nasal_palatal_approximant" title="Nasal palatal approximant">\n         nasal palatal approximant\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\n         <a href="/wiki/Nasal_palatal_approximant" title="Nasal palatal approximant">\n          j\xcc\x83\n         </a>\n         ]\n        </span>\n        , which\n        <a href="/wiki/Nasalization" title="Nasalization">\n         nasalizes\n        </a>\n        the vowel that precedes it:\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xcb\x88n\xc4\xa9j\xcc\x83u]\n        </span>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n         <a href="#cite_note-112">\n          [112]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n         <a href="#cite_note-113">\n          [113]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="#CITEREFBisol2005">\n         Bisol (2005\n        </a>\n        :122) proposes that Portuguese possesses labio-velar stops\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /k\xca\xb7/\n        </span>\n        and\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /\xc9\xa1\xca\xb7/\n        </span>\n        as additional phonemes rather than sequences of a velar stop and\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /w/\n        </span>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-labialized_velar_-_Bisol_109-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-labialized_velar_-_Bisol-109">\n          [109]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The consonant hereafter denoted as\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /\xca\x81/\n        </span>\n        has a variety of realizations depending on dialect. In Europe, it is typically a\n        <a href="/wiki/Uvular_trill" title="Uvular trill">\n         uvular trill\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xca\x80]\n        </span>\n        ; however, a pronunciation as a\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_uvular_fricative" title="Voiced uvular fricative">\n         voiced uvular fricative\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xca\x81]\n        </span>\n        may be becoming dominant in urban areas. There is also a realization as a\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">\n         voiceless uvular fricative\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xcf\x87]\n        </span>\n        , and the original pronunciation as an\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">\n         alveolar trill\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [r]\n        </span>\n        also remains very common in various dialects.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n         <a href="#cite_note-114">\n          [114]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        A common realization of the word-initial\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /r/\n        </span>\n        in the Lisbon accent is a voiced uvular trill fricative\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_raised_uvular_trill" title="Voiced raised uvular trill">\n          \xca\x80\xcc\x9d\n         </a>\n         ]\n        </span>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gr157_115-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-gr157-115">\n          [115]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        In Brazil,\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /\xca\x81/\n        </span>\n        can be\n        <a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">\n         velar\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Uvular_consonant" title="Uvular consonant">\n         uvular\n        </a>\n        , or\n        <a href="/wiki/Glottal_consonant" title="Glottal consonant">\n         glottal\n        </a>\n        and may be voiceless unless between voiced sounds;\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n         <a href="#cite_note-116">\n          [116]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        it is usually pronounced as a\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">\n         voiceless velar fricative\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [x]\n        </span>\n        , a\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">\n         voiceless glottal fricative\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [h]\n        </span>\n        or\n        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">\n         voiceless uvular fricative\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xcf\x87]\n        </span>\n        . See also\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Guttural_R#Portuguese" title="Guttural R">\n          Guttural R in Portuguese\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /s/\n        </span>\n        and\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /z/\n        </span>\n        are normally\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lamino-alveolar_consonant" title="Lamino-alveolar consonant">\n         lamino-alveolar\n        </a>\n        , as in English. However, a number of dialects in northern Portugal pronounce\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /s/\n        </span>\n        and\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /z/\n        </span>\n        as\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apico-alveolar" title="Apico-alveolar">\n         apico-alveolar\n        </a>\n        <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">\n         sibilants\n        </a>\n        (sounding somewhat like a soft\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xca\x83]\n        </span>\n        or\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xca\x92]\n        </span>\n        ), as in the Romance languages of northern Iberia. A very few northeastern Portugal dialects still maintain the medieval distinction between apical and laminal sibilants (written\n        <i>\n         s/ss\n        </i>\n        and\n        <i>\n         c/\xc3\xa7/z\n        </i>\n        , respectively).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        As a phoneme,\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /t\xca\x83/\n        </span>\n        only occurs in loanwords, with a tendency for speakers to substitute in\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /\xca\x83/\n        </span>\n        . However,\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [t\xca\x83]\n        </span>\n        is an\n        <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">\n         allophone\n        </a>\n        of\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /t/\n        </span>\n        before\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /i/\n        </span>\n        in a number of Brazilian dialects. Similarly,\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [d\xca\x92]\n        </span>\n        is an allophone of\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /d/\n        </span>\n        in the same contexts.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        In northern and central Portugal, the voiced stops\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /b/\n        </span>\n        ,\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /d/\n        </span>\n        ,\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         /\xc9\xa1/\n        </span>\n        are usually lenited to\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fricative" title="Fricative">\n         fricatives\n        </a>\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xce\xb2]\n        </span>\n        ,\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xc3\xb0]\n        </span>\n        , and\n        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n         [\xc9\xa3]\n        </span>\n        respectively, except at the beginning of words, or after nasal vowels;\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n         <a href="#cite_note-117">\n          [117]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n         <a href="#cite_note-118">\n          [118]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        a\n        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology#Phonetic_notes" title="Spanish phonology">\n         similar process\n        </a>\n        occurs in Spanish.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">\n        Grammar\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Grammar">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_grammar" title="Portuguese grammar">\n        Portuguese grammar\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A notable aspect of the grammar of Portuguese is the verb. Morphologically, more verbal inflections from classical Latin have been preserved by Portuguese than by any other major\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">\n        Romance language\n       </a>\n       . The Portuguese and Spanish grammars are very close. It also has some innovations not found in other Romance languages (except Galician and the Fala):\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Present_perfect" title="Present perfect">\n         present perfect\n        </a>\n        has an iterative sense unique to the Galician-Portuguese language group. It denotes an action or a series of actions that began in the past and are expected to keep repeating in the future. For instance, the sentence\n        <i>\n         Tenho tentado falar com ela\n        </i>\n        would be translated to "I have been trying to talk to her", not "I have tried to talk to her". On the other hand, the correct translation of the question "Have you heard the latest news?" is not\n        <i>\n         *Tem ouvido a \xc3\xbaltima not\xc3\xadcia?\n        </i>\n        , but\n        <i>\n         Ouviu a \xc3\xbaltima not\xc3\xadcia?\n        </i>\n        , since no repetition is implied.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n         <a href="#cite_note-119">\n          [119]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">\n         Vernacular\n        </a>\n        Portuguese still uses the future\n        <a href="/wiki/Subjunctive_mood" title="Subjunctive mood">\n         subjunctive mood\n        </a>\n        , which developed from medieval\n        <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">\n         West Iberian Romance\n        </a>\n        and in present-day Spanish and Galician has almost entirely fallen into disuse. The future subjunctive appears in dependent clauses that denote a condition that must be fulfilled in the future so that the independent clause will occur. English normally employs the present tense under the same circumstances:\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         Se eu\n        </i>\n        for\n        <i>\n         eleito presidente, mudarei a lei.\n        </i>\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        If\n        <i>\n         I should be\n        </i>\n        elected president, I will change the law.\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         Quando\n        </i>\n        fores\n        <i>\n         mais velho, vais entender.\n        </i>\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        When\n        <i>\n         you grow\n        </i>\n        older, you will understand.\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The personal\n        <a href="/wiki/Infinitive" title="Infinitive">\n         infinitive\n        </a>\n        : infinitives can\n        <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">\n         inflect\n        </a>\n        according to their subject in\n        <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">\n         person\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">\n         number\n        </a>\n        , often showing who is expected to perform a certain action; cf.\n        <i>\n         \xc3\x89 melhor voltares\n        </i>\n        "It is better [for you] to go back",\n        <i>\n         \xc3\x89 melhor voltarmos\n        </i>\n        "It is better [for us] to go back." Perhaps for this reason, infinitive clauses replace subjunctive clauses more often in Portuguese than in other Romance languages.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">\n        Writing system\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Writing system">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table cellpadding="4" cellspacing="0" class="infobox bordered" style="width:250px; font-size:95%; float:right; float:right;">\n       <caption>\n        <big>\n         <b>\n          Written varieties\n         </b>\n        </big>\n       </caption>\n       <tr>\n        <th style="background:#ddd;">\n         Portugal and non-1990 Agreement countries\n        </th>\n        <th style="background:#ddd;">\n         Brazil and 1990 Agreement countries\n        </th>\n        <th style="background:#ddd;">\n         translation\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         dire\n         <b>\n          c\n         </b>\n         \xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         dire\xc3\xa7\xc3\xa3o\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         direction\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         \xc3\xb3\n         <b>\n          p\n         </b>\n         timo\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xc3\xb3timo\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         best, excellent, optimal\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">\n        Portuguese orthography\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Portuguese is written with 26 letters of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">\n        Latin script\n       </a>\n       , making use of five\n       <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">\n        diacritics\n       </a>\n       to denote stress, vowel height, contraction, nasalization, and etymological\n       <a href="/wiki/Assibilation" title="Assibilation">\n        assibilation\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">\n        acute accent\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Circumflex" title="Circumflex">\n        circumflex\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Grave_accent" title="Grave accent">\n        grave accent\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tilde" title="Tilde">\n        tilde\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cedilla" title="Cedilla">\n        cedilla\n       </a>\n       ). The\n       <a href="/wiki/Diaeresis_(diacritic)" title="Diaeresis (diacritic)">\n        trema\n       </a>\n       was also formerly used in Brazilian Portuguese, and can still be encountered in words derived from proper names in other languages, such as Anhang\xc3\xbcera and m\xc3\xbclleriano.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Accented characters and\n       <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">\n        digraphs\n       </a>\n       are not counted as separate letters for\n       <a href="/wiki/Collation" title="Collation">\n        collation\n       </a>\n       purposes.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spelling_reforms">\n        Spelling reforms\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Spelling reforms">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Reforms_of_Portuguese_orthography" title="Reforms of Portuguese orthography">\n        Reforms of Portuguese orthography\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span     <span style="margin:0 0.5em">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Guinea-Bissau.svg">\n            <img alt="Flag of Guinea-Bissau.svg" data-file-height="600"
